O, sons, because I have completed this book for you, which is the last of the science of medicine, for the fulfillment of it, its consequence is found in it, and for the exposures of it, and for the declarations of it, it is my vision that you complete it with this treatise, which is a part of the operation with my hand, so it is surgery.
Because the operation with the hand is widespread in our region and in our time completely private, whereas many risk the science of it, and its knowledge is held hostage; and there remain of it only some small descriptions in the books of the Ancients, which are muddled and become subject to those errors and uncertainties, because within their clauses the understandings of it are and the force of it and the art are elongated.
And it is seen to me that you bring that to life with the order of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and for that it comes with the forms of the tools of cautery and of the other instruments of the work, as it is for the addition of the declaration, and for the preparation of it, which cause is necessary.
But the cause for which no good artificer with his hand is found in this our time, is because the art of medicine is long, and that he who acts it must before that be exercised in the science of anatomy, which reconciles Gualia within that he knows the joints of the members and the forms of those, and the conjunction and the separation of theirs; and he should have the knowledge of the bones, the nerves and the cartilages, the number of those, and the egress of theirs; and of the pulsatile veins and the quiet ones, and the places of the emission of theirs.
And for that, it is said by Hippocrates that with a name it is not much, but in the work it is little, and most in the art of the hand.
But we have already said of that in the introduction of this book; because whoever is not aware of what we have said of anatomy, it is not evacuated that he does not fall into error for which many men die, so as I have seen too many of those, because some are formed in this science and throw themselves away from that knowledge and their experiments.
Because I saw a foolish and inexperienced physician who had incised an abscess scrophilos in the neck of a woman, and incised some arteries of the neck so that much blood flowed while the woman died among the hands of him.
And I saw another physician who thought that the throat of a man who had been processed in his state should be treated with a stone, and the stone was large, and it came to him and extracted that stone with a piece of the bladder, for that man on the third day died.
And I had already been called to extract that, and I saw that because of the size of the stone and the disposition of the patient, I knew on him that he would die.
And I saw another physician who took a stipend from a duke of our land for surgery, and he undertook a black crutch who was broken in his thigh; and prepared the physician with his ignorance, extracted the fracture, on the wound, with splints and splints with strong structure, and did not leave the wound to breathe.
And then he dismissed him according to his desires, and then he relieved him, and then he left him for some days and commanded that we untie the ligament; and it happened so that the thigh and the foot became infected with an abscess, and it came to ruin.
And I was called to him, and I prepared to untie the ligament, and obtained the tranquility and then he was freed from his pains.
But however, the corruption was already confirmed in the limb, for that I could not restrain it, and it did not cease to wander the corruption in the limb until the patient perished.
And I saw another physician who perforated a cancerous abscess, and it was ulcerated after some days, until the malice of it was magnified to its lord.
The cause of which is because the cancerous caut is pure of melancholic humor, therefore it does not come to it with iron at all, but that it should be in a limb that suffers that it be entirely held hostage.
And therefore, sons, it is necessary for you that the operation with the hand be devised into two divisions: so it is in the operation to which health is associated, and in the work with which there is peril in the major dispositions.
And I have already exerted this in all places of this book in which I come to operation in which there is error and fear; because it is necessary for you that you guard this and leave that, so that the foolish ones do not attain a way to speak and to dishonor you.
And therefore, take your arms with solicitude and with the protection of God, and your patients with facility and with firmness.
And use the best way by the grace of God, pursuing health and laudable success, and leave the terrible ailments of difficult healing, and keep your arms from that which makes you fear, so that hesitation in your faith and in your name does not escape you: because more is remaining to your glory, and more in the world and in the hereafter to your sanctities.
Gualia already said in some of his admonitions: “Do not treat a bad disease, so that you are not called bad physicians.”
And now I have divided this book according to three chapters.
Begins the division of the book, and the first of the first part. The first chapter ordered within feet, in the forms of the instruments and in the tools of the cauteries, and of what is necessary in the operation.
The division of the second part. The second chapter, of suction and perforation, and of leeches, and of poultices, and of the extraction of arrows and of things similar to those, all chaptered and ordered of the forms of the instruments.
The third chapter, of restoration and dislocation, and of the cure of sprains and of things similar to those; chapter ordered of the head within feet, and of the forms of the instruments.
Know that you should say the quality of the judgments of that cautery and of its inconveniences, and in what complexion cautery is prohibited.
Therefore I say that the discourse of the quality of the judgment of cautery and of its inconveniences is a long and prolix discourse, and subtle by science, and secretly hidden; and already of it many wise men have spoken, and of it they have disagreed, and to me a little of the discourses of theirs suffices, fearing prolixity.
And therefore I say that cautery agrees to all complexions universally which is with matter or its matter, except two complexions, which are complexions hot of its matter.
In the hot and dry complexion with matter they disagree; for some say that cautery is beneficial to that, and others say the contrary of that, that cautery is not convenient in illness which is by quality and by dryness, because the nature of fire is quality and dryness, and inconvenient is that illness hot and dry with that which is caut and dry be healed.
And they say that who says the contrary of that, that by cautery is made benefit in all hot and dry illness that comes in the bodies of men, because when you compare the body of man and its humidities to the complexion of fire, you find the body of man cold.
And I say for the discourse of that, that experience this already to me some times has discovered.
But however, it should not come upon that which already is explored and exercised in the chapter of cautery by the previous exercise, and who has known the diversity of the complexion of men and the disposition of the illnesses in their own bodies, and the causes of those, and their accidents, and the expanse of time of those.
But in the other complexions, there is no fear over you, and more so in the cold and humid illnesses, because already all the physicians have agreed upon those, and they do not disagree in the judgment with cautery in those.
And know, sons, that of the secret of cure by cautery with fire and of the goodness of it, it is because fire is simple, the action of which does not reach beyond the member which is cauterized and does not reach the other member joined to it except with little inconvenience.
But the action of burning medicine reaches that in the members which are far from it, and it makes them come to the member illness of difficult healing and often worse.
But fire, by its sublimity and of its substance goodness, does not do that except to superfluously. And it is already known to us by experience and by length of service of study in the art about the truth of the causes; and for that I am excused of the length of the discourse, and if it were not that it is not written in my book in this place to you a secret hidden with fire, and the quality of its operation in the bodies and of its expulsion by which expels the illnesses, with a philosophical and demonstrative discourse, which would be acute in your minds.
And know, sons, that they disagree about the time in which it is convenient to do cautery and they pause the best time of spring.
And I say that cautery is convenient at all times, because so that the inconvenience for the accidental time is submerged in the benefit of that which with the cautery is thrown, and more so if the cautery is for pains or of necessary pains, strong and fistulas, which do not suffer delay because it is feared of those that come malice, which is greater than little inconvenience entering for time.
And therefore do not catch in your minds, o sons, that this is not esteemed by the vulgar people and the foolish physicians, because it is that to that illness that is healed by cautery is not reduced at all times, and they pause that consequence.
And the cause is not so as they care about that, because cautery is not but in place of medicine which alters the complexion and dries the humidities which are the cause for which pains come.
But however, cautery superfluously over medicine by the will of its validity and virtue of its operation and greatness of its lord.
And it is possible that its illness returns at some time of the time, according to the complexion of the patient and the location of its illness, and the virtue of it, and what is prepared in the body of it of the aggregation of the superfluities in it, and what has reached it in its acquisition in foods and things similar to those causes; unless that the illness in which cautery is administered is a subtle illness in a member of few superfluities and humidities, as cautery of teeth for pain and things similar to that, it is possible that in it it does not return that pain, but it is done in small.
And most common speech is that cautery is the last remedy of medicine, and it is true speech, not that I understand it in it, because I think that there is no cure that benefits with medicine nor with any other cause except cautery.
And the cause is the opposite of that; and the understanding that cautery is the last remedy of medicine is only when they administer the healing methods in some diseases, and those medicines do not confer, and then at the end of the cause man administers cautery, and it benefits to that. And therefore it is said that cautery is the last remedy of medicine, not according to the understanding which I understand the common people and many foolish doctors.
And the ancients said that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron, and they did not say this except for the equality of gold and the sublimity of its substance.
And they said that the place of cautery does not make a scar, as it is not absolutely true, because I have already seen that and have found that it does not do so except in some bodies that have others, and cautery with that is good and better than with iron as they said; however, when you do cautery with fire with gold, it is not declared to you, because it is ignited according to the quantity that you want for the roar of the gold, and that it prepares to receive heat; and if you adjust over it ignition, the gold melts for the fire, and in the fire some sheets so that the artisan catches for the occupation of that.
And for that reason cautery with iron must be done more lightly and more carefully to the rectitude of operation.
And I have already ordered this chapter on cautery according to chapters, and I have ordered those of the head within the feet, so that later the demander asks for that from it.
The first chapter.
This cauterization confers on the humidity and cold over the nerve accident of which there are two causes, so it is the cause of soda and multitude of rheumatic flux, called corissa, from the head to the parts of the eyes and ears it flows, and multitude of sleeping, and pain of teeth and of the goiter, and universally of all sickness that comes from cold, as well as paralytically, soda and apoplexy, and similar in those diseases.
The form of this cauterization is this, that first you command the patient to be evacuated with laxative medicine the head modifying, for three or for four nights, according to that it requires the virtue of the sickness and the age of him and his custom.
And then command him to shave his head, and then do that seizure between your hands on a chair laid down and that he place his hands on his feet.
And then place the razor of your palm near the nose between his eyebrows. But however, as the your word of the middle place is arrived, sign that place with a ten, and then ignite the cautery olive of which this is the form:
And then place that upon the place signed with a ten, in the manner that it descends, with which your hand be constricted little by little, and you revolve that.
And then lift your hand slightly and look at the place, and if you see already of the bone being uncovered some quantity of the head, as well as the quantity of grain of ears, then raise your hand, and if not return your hand with that iron, with another of that, if it is cooled, until it is seen of the bone that I have told you.
And then take a little salt and dissolve that on the place and leave that for three days.
And then place on it a cloth soaked in butter and leave that on it until the scar of the fire is destroyed. And then cure the place with tetrafarmacon ointment until it is healed.
And they already said that when the plague remains open, so much better gets the scar, because it is better and more helpful.
And they said some of them that the spine be cauterized into the bone, and be held the cautery until some part of the surface of the bone be burned.
And then be scraped that which is burned of the bone, and then be cured.
And they said others that with the cautery reach the back, until it presses in the bone strong pressure until the bone breaks, and this is the form of alphecati small: And they estimate of that place expire the vapors of the head.
And be kept the plague open for long time, and then be cured until it is consolidated.
But to me no have been seen these two species of cautery of all, but in some men according to way of fear; and leave that, of me, better is with health, when it is; because the head is developed by solution of continuity of it as well as we have testified in the other members, and more so when the head of the patient is of cold nature.
And the species of cautery first is more safe and better of me; and of that use and with that work with health.
Second chapter.
Of the cautery of the head.
When chronic and prolonged pain occurs throughout the head and it is prolonged in the patient, and use of poultices and compresses and capipulges and plasters and guats and cadels and gualinas and semblances, and mostly if it is already cauterized with a cautery which recounts and does not benefit him from any of those causes, then consider that if the head of the patient is of strong creation in its nature; and is not frail and finds a great deal of heat, then cauterize him with another cautery than the one before. And then cauterize that on the corner of his head with a cautery until the skin is parted. Incise the skin and uncover the quantity which we have recounted and cauterize that with a cautery in the back part of the head in the place which is called vas, — and that is the place in which is placed a cupping glass. And alleviate your hand in doing so, and do not uncover the bone, because the patient by this feels a great deal of pain different from the pain of all the other cauteries of the head.
And you say this cautery in its place, because whoever cauterizes the horns of the head and the occiput with the cautery which is more subtle than that with which the middle part of the head is cauterized; and this is the form of it.
Chapter Three.
Of cauterization of an old hernia.
When there is a sudden pain in the side of the head, or pain that extends into the eye, it should be evacuated with medicines that modify the head, and the other cure should be administered, which I have said in the divisions of the ailments; and if nothing helps, then the cauterization in it is in two ways: either cauterization with acute and burning medicine, or with iron.
But cauterization with burning medicine is that you take a piece of alum, and scrape that and cut off the extremities of it from both ends. And then incise the place of the pain in the temple with a lancet until it is in it made a place after the skin, until it is hidden.
And then strengthen over it with a stopper for descent constriction, and leave that for the space of three hours; and then untie the and take off the alum, and leave the ulcer for two or three days, and then place over it a poultice submerged in butter until the place makes a scab.
And then cure that with a gargle until it is healed.
And if you wish, do this with some burning medicines which I have written in the two treatises of burning medicines.
But cauterization with iron according to this manner:  ignite a cautery of which this is the form:
and it is called a clove cautery, because the head of it is as the form of a clove in which there is some curvature, and in the middle part of it is a small eminence.
And then place over the place of the pain, and hold your hand — so that the artery which is below is not burned — and revolve the iron little by little with speed.
And if the quantity of it that is burned by the thickness of the skin as much as the majority of it, and elevate your hand so that the artery below is not burned, so that there does not come a flow of blood.
And then imbibe a poultice in salt water and place that over the place, and leave that for three days; and then place a poultice mashed with butter, and then cure with a gargle until it is healed.
And if you wish, cauterize with the extremity of the knife cautery, and guard yourself from incision of the artery in this hernia properly old.
Chapter Four.

However, it is necessary for you to guard against the continuation of the jawbone, which is bad for chewing, and that the nerve that feels that, and that it does not become a spasm.
And if it is about the custody and caution of the flow of blood from the artery that is incised, because in the incision of it there is fear, and most to him who ignores what is done and is not studious and experienced; and leaves the operation in him at the beginning.
And I will come with a remembrance of the regiment of blood flow accident of the artery according to its manner, in its place of this book.

Chapter V.
Of cauterization of the pains of the ears.
When in the ear there is pain by fire and it is cured with laxative causes and with the other cure which I have said in the division, and the pain is not removed, then ignite the cautery, and this is the one which has a point, of which this is the form:

And if the cautery of ten points in the whole ear, and that one, and then cure the places while they are healing.
Chapter VI.
Of cauterization of the tumor.
Tumor which is cured and with cauterization is only of the kinds which come by phlegm, according to what we have said in the divisions of the diseases.
Avoid cauterization of the species that should come from dryness or spasm of the nerve.
When you cure that species of tumor with herbs and purgatives and gargles, and if you do not comfort your cure, then when you cauterize the tumor with three cauteries: the first you must the root of the ear, the second a little below its temple, and the third you must the junction of the two lips.
And pause your cautery for the opposite side of the sick part, because softening does not come except in the part that is healthy.
And the form of cauterization is that you cauterize that with the cautery in the right of the extremity of the ear more sovereign a little above the horn of the head, and in the temple another, the length of which be according to the length of the said finger, and pause your hand with cautery while the quantity of the majority of the species of the codena is burned.

Chapter X.
Of cauterization of epilepsy.
An epileptic is not cauterized, but rather that epilepsy is due to phlegm.
And therefore, whoever modifies the brain of him at the beginning of him with years and with the other cure which we have said in the division when the patient is great and is tolerating the excess of the medicines.

Chapter XVI.
Of cautery of the eyelid of the eye when the hairs are converted to the parts of the eyelids and pierce the eye.
When the hairs of the eye are converted to the parts of the eyelids so that they pierce the eye, cauterize in those in two manners, whether cauterize or is with a burning medicine.
If with cautery of it with fire, command the patient in front of it that he pluck his hairs as those which they pluck them, until they are prolonged and equal; and if you pierce that of them, then you strengthen the eyes of him with a bandage so that it may not be bad until the hairs are born.
Therefore, as they are born and equal, then place the head of the patient in your knee, and then send over the eyelid of the eyes of him with a tent, with a sign which is according to the figure of a leaf of myrtle, and be the beginning of the sign near the hairs.

Chapter XVII.
Of cauterization of a fistula that is in the tear duct of the eye.
When you cure a fistula with what we have said in the divisions of the diseases and do not confer your cure, then you must cauterize it according to this manner: command the patient to place his head in your lap, and have some minister hold his head between your hands in such a way that it is not moved or agitated by his head.
Then place a cloth soaked in hot water or in a poultice of ptilli on the eye of him.
And then ignite the cautery of which this is the form:
which is concave, as is the shape of a cane or a vulture's feather, at one end of which the cautery is made.
And if you wish, it may be penetrating into the other end. And if you wish, it may be sorted as it tends.
But nevertheless, the one that is concave is better for your work.
And then press the fistula if it is open, and draw out from it pus and dry it up. And if it is not open, then open it and extract the pus from it.

But if ten days had passed and it is not healed, then place on it a sharp corrosive medicine until the bone is uncovered and is scraped according to what you have ordained in your chapter.
And there is another way of cauterizing a fistula which some first said:  enter into the place of the fistula and cut it open, and then place in that fissure a fine thread of which this is the shape: And put into it the quantity of one ounce of melted lead; and hold your hand with a good hold, and do not move the patient so that the melted lead does not reach the eye of him; and cover the eye of the patient with a cloth soaked in hot water or in water, for the lead will burn the place of the fistula and heal it by a miraculous healing.

Chapter XX.
Of cauterization of the teeth and softening of the gums.

Chapter XXI.
Of cauterization of tooth pain.
When tooth pain is due to coldness, or a worm is in it, or the cure does not agree with medicine, then cauterize it in one of these two ways: with a cautery of cow's hide, or with a cautery of fire.
Cauterizing with hide is that you take the hide of cows and boil it in a cauldron of iron, and then take a stick and wrap it around the tip of the cautery, and then immerse that in the boiled hide, and place it on the painful tooth, quickly, until it is burned.
And then repeat that several times until the virtue of the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, submerge wool or a stick in the above-mentioned hide, and place it on the painful tooth, and place a red-hot iron above it until the iron reaches the tip of the cavity of the tooth.
But however, cauterization with fire is that you wait for the tip of the iron or of the cautery to be somewhat thick and the sharpness of the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient.
And then ignite the cautery, the shape of which will come, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand over it until the cautery is burned; and do this several times until the pain is subdued, either on that day or the next.
And cover that with the patient's mouth with good hide, and keep it there for an hour, and then spit it out; and this is the shape of the cautery.
And cauterize with whichever extremity you wish, according to what is possible for you.
And this is the shape of the cannula:

Chapter .xlviii.

Chapter .xlix.

Chapter .l.

Chapter .lii.
Of cauterization of corrodents.
Corrodent is a corruption that walks in the limb, which corrodes it as fire consumes dry wood.

Therefore, as it is expelled, then you distill into the wool water cauda in which you have mixed honey or water in which you have already boiled fennel and honey.
And then cure it with the other causes until it is healed.
Chapter XXII.
Of the cure of the descending water of the wool.
We have already said the species of the water in the division and which you should pierce with a sermon declaring, then this according to the health.
Then you must make the patient sit between your hands on a cushion and tie his wool, tightening it.
And then place your left hand near the eyelid of his wool, if the wool in which is the water is the left; or on your right hand, if the wool is the right.
And then with your right hand take the almond, if the wool is left; or with your left hand, if the wool is right.
And then place the tip of the almond near the crown for the thickness of the ray in the album of the wool from the side of the lacrimal gland, and then press the almond with virtue and roll your hand with it.
And then penetrate into the album of the wool and feel that the almond has already reached the void cause.
And it must be the measure of the path of the almond to the tip the measure of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the black, and it is the crown of the wool; for you will see with that pupil in the vision of the wool by the clarity of the cornea tunic.
And then place the almond into the place where is the water, and then you throw it down once, and then if the water descends so quickly, then vetz the patient water over which he covers his sight immediately, and almond in his wool.
And then rest for a while; then if the water has descended, then you remove that other time as long as the almond is not thrown.
And then when it is dried and does not descend, then you extract the almond with ease, and roll with it your hand little by little, and then dissolve in the water a little clear salt of gemma and with that wash the wool from within; and then place outside the wool cotto or stopa or wool infused in rose oil and egg white and lick with water the wool of it.
But not those who are of our time place on that commi trissat with egg white.
And if you do not obey your almond to the entrance of the wool because of its hardness — for it is some men whose wool is very hard — then you must take the spatula which is called alberid of which this is the form:
And then pierce with that that juncture, and do not end your hand in the trace, and it is not if you do not make way for the almond place subtle.
And then introduce the almond as we have said.
And you must complete the work, be prepared for the patient to sleep comfortably in a bed made in a dark room, and be prohibited from all movements.
And keep him in nature so that his nature is cleansed, and do not turn his head to the right or left at all.
And bind him according to his disposition within the third day.
And after, in that dark room, remove the bandage and expose the foot, and have him see some causes, and then return the bandage within the seventh day.
And do not allow him to do this during the hour of the cures or immediately after the infusion. It is necessary that you avoid this because the water can pass lightly through the great and vehement of regard.
But if an abscess occurs, then you must unbind the wound before the seventh day, and rectify it with water that drains the abscess.
Then you shall cover the sight of him and place upon his face an oral for which the movement of him shall be regulated, leaving him for several days, he existing in the dark room.
And then he shall be taken out of that room gradually and conversed about his causes.
And know that in alchemy the disciple of vision is not excused sometimes, and then you shall be bold about the operation.
And we have already come to some of those who are in the Artach, and some say that they made fire in the Ayrac magdaam perforated with which water is sucked.
But however, I have not seen in our land any who had perfect water, nor have I read water in some of the books of the ancients; and it is possible that this is novel.
And these are the forms of the species of magdaam so that it is upon those those who ignore those:
And they are made of eram or iron properly, and their extremities are with this triangular subtlety, the acute extremity as such is the form.
Chapter XXIV.
Of the cure of flesh wounds in the nose.
When in the nose are born diverse flesh growths, of which some cause is assembled like a scorpion of motz pes, or a polyp pes; and this malady is called polyp because it is similar to that pes represented. And of it is cancerous flesh, lapadea, of dusky color; and of it is that flesh leon not of dusky color.
Therefore, in that which is in these leon flesh not fraudulent nor cancerous, you must make the patient sit between your hands and put him in the sun, and  dry his nostrils, and pick your onci in those flesh. And then extract that to the outward parts, and then incise the water that you have comprehended of those with a sharp, subtle spatula on one side, until you know that all the flesh is gone; if any cause of it remains, of which the abscision is possible, then you root out that with one of the subtle instruments with ease, until none of it remains. But if it bleeds or an abscess occurs, then you pause to him that which you must; or if it is of the malignant abscesses, then you cut and cauterize it until it is abscised blood and all the cavities are gone.
And then be placed in the nose after the incision vi agree and water or wine. But if the nose is open and from it proceeds humidity into the palate, then you know that it is already healed.
But if the humidity does not penetrate as it should, then you know that deep within him is flesh wound in the pus surpluses bones of the nose to which abscision has not reached.
Therefore, then you must introduce a file into him of which there is some thickness, and place in it motz nuts, and place between each nut the quantity of the finger or less, and engage the patient and introduce one extremity of the file into the nose with the ray or with another cause which is to him possible.
And as soon as this is done, that he may throw his odor into it until it reaches the canals of the nose, and be spit upon his golayro, because troops of times the semblance to this action do the children at the schools, and it is easier cause to him who wants to do it.
And then place the two extremities of the file, one extremity that goes out over the nose and the other that remains in the nose, and then administer a serration of flesh with the nuts that are in the file, and do this until you know that the flesh is already with the nuts of the file.
And then extract the file, and place in the nose after the abstraction of blood a poultice, and do this for three days or more until the engent corrodes all that is remaining of the flesh.
And at the end of the cause, place in the nose a lead pipe for several days until it is healed.
But if you need a cure that requires, use that.
And this is the form of the instrument a capipurge maker with which oils and medicines are distilled in the nose:
And make it of silver or of iron, which is similar to a small open lamp, as a small conch, and the meat similarly.
And if you wish, make a closed cannula like a tube, and the cannula of the instrument to be used for purging is flat, uncovered; to which handle at the back of it, with which you hold it when you heat oil or water in it of the succus and of the suckable causes.
Chapter XXV.
Of the eels natz in the limbs of the nose.
Many things are said about the eel natz in the limbs of the nose, and it is magnified and mentioned on certain days in which the regard of it is not read.

But if its incision is delayed until it is magnified, then consider if it is calcified, hard, of a dusky color and of little feeling, then do not touch that with iron for it is a cranky abscess; for many things are said about that one who incides this abscess should be in great malice upon him who had it.
And if the abscess is of a lion's touch and is not of a dusky color, and times that incision is possible in all of that, then evacuate the patient and incise that without fear, and cure the spot with water that exsudes and constrict within which it is healed.
Chapter XXVI.
Of the suture of the nose and of the lips and of the ear when the continuity is dissolved by plague or by resemblances.
Know that when accidents dissolve continuity in one of these cartilages, few confer in that operation unless in some men.
Therefore, when it is necessary to have some cause of those, consider if it is fresh plague with its blood, and then you adjust the two lips of the plague with suture, and then cure that until it is healed.
And if the lips of the solution of continuity are already separated, and each one is made healthy, then it is necessary that you excoriate each part of its apparent code until blood escapes. And then adjust the two lips with suture and strengthen those, and over those pulverize blood of dragon and incense, and place over the powder a piece of diafinicon plaster, or of some other of the consolidating plasters, and leave that tied for two days or three, and then untie that and change that plaster and leave it until the threads are by themselves abscinditz, and then cure with an enguent until it is healed.
But the manner of the suture is that you add the solution of continuity or with needles as we have recommended in the suture of the belly, or add the solution of continuity with thread as to you and have it known.
Chapter XXVII.
Of extraction of those causes that come in the two lips in the parts between them.
Many things are said about many men in the parts between their lips some abscesses hard resembling fat of worms, and some of them are smaller and some are larger.

Chapter XXVIII.
Of incision of the flesh adjusted in the gums.
Great many things are said about the flesh adjusted in the gums which the ancients called albulus, therefore it is necessary that you suspend that with an ounce or that you have that with the forceps and incision that you must cut its root, and let the sania run or the blood.
And then place on the spot incense blood or other stiptic or excicative powders.
And if that flesh returns, then incise that secondarily, and cauterize that, for then the cautery will not return.
Chapter XXIX.
Of reason of teeth with iron.

Chapter .xxx.
Of the Eradication of Teeth.
Know that you cure the tooth of its pain with all care and take time in its entire eradication, for there is no cause that should supplant the whiteness of it when it is eradicated, for it is a sublime substance within that which is excused in its eradication.
But know when the patient is forced to have that tooth eradicated, that firmly you must certify which tooth is the painful one, for often the pain deceives the patient and leads you to believe it is in a healthy tooth, and you eradicate that one and the pain does not cease until the bad and painful tooth is eradicated, for we have already seen this by the operation of the barbers.
Therefore, as you must certify which tooth is the painful one, and that you know well, then know that you must scarify in the circuit of the tooth with a spatula in which there is some virtue, until it is dissolved from the tooth of the gum of all parts, and then with your own fingers, or with subtle forceps at the beginning little by little until that you concucesquas.
And then, with a strong hold, take large pliers for good articulation or strong stupor, and place the patient's head between your teeth which you hold well so that it does not harm, and then pull the tooth according to rectitude in a manner that you do not break it, nor give the patient greater pain.
And therefore if it is not forgotten, then take one of those instruments, and put that one under it from all parts with facility and exert the removal of it as it was done at the beginning.
But if the tooth is broken or corroded, then know that you must compress of cloth that broken and tighten that with the extremity of a subtle ray so that it not be broken in the hour of your constriction upon it with pliers.
And know that you must work exquisitely with scarification in the circuit of all parts of the gum and guard well your strength that you do not break that and remain a part of it, and return upon the patient for the malice that it may be greater than the first pain of it.
And guard yourself that you do not do what some ignorant barbers do in their fistination and audacity upon the eradication of theirs, for they do not administer what we have recommended; for often times they bring upon men maladies great ones which are more difficult to be broken, and the roots of theirs remaugulated all, or some of those, or that which you extract those with some bones of the mandible as well as many times we have testified.
And after the eradication of it, the mouth be washed with wine caut or wine agre with salt.
And if it behooveth flux of blood thereby, as many times it behooveth, then take some quantity of zegi and sprinkle it upon the wound, and if you do not confer that zegi, cauterize.
The form of the forceps and subtle pliers with which the tooth is bad at the beginning be of long extremity, of short handle and thick, so that they not be bent when with those you must work.
And be as times of thick handle so that when you tighten with those they not be bent, be short extremities.
And be made of Indian iron descentment made of straight extremities, and in the extremities of those be teeth of which some intrude in the others and tighten by strong constriction descent, and some times the extremities of those be the form of the beak of a bird which has name ciconia, so it is guanta, and they are of strong constriction.

Chapter .xxxii.
Of the cure of the teeth eminent above the others.
When the teeth are eminent not according to their natural course, for those the form is laid, and mostly when it befalls to women, and mostly to the venerable old ones; therefore, as you consider: if a tooth is nothing near another tooth, and it is not possible to suture or liniment it, then root that; but that it is not annexed to another tooth, then you incise that with this instrument of which this is the form; and it is similar to a pig's snout, and it is made of Indian iron of a sharp end.
And let your incision be with which you incise that in too many days because of the hardness of the tooth, and that it is not gnawed by another of the teeth.
And if the eminent tooth is exposed to filing, then file that with a file of Indian iron of which this is the form:
And let it all be of Indian iron and the margin be well-made; and let it be of very small points as well as a file with which needles are made, with which the tooth be filed little by little in many days with ease, so that no other tooth is gnawed and broken. And then line that at the end, and root that with some razors.
And if it is a tooth of which one part is pierced and it lies the tongue, then as you file that until the projection of that fracture be stayed and leveled, and be filled so that the tongue does not touch it and the word does not break.
Chapter .xxxiii.
Of the restoration of teeth damaged with gold or silver filings.
When accidents happen to the teeth in front with concussion and removal by percussion or by fall, and the patient cannot bear what he eats, and you have cured that with styptic medicines, and it has not been of any use, then for that no decay is engendered in those that are strengthened with gold filings and not with silver, because silver becomes green and soon, but gold never changes.
And let the filings be in such subtlety and thickness according to the quantity that can enter between the teeth; and the form of the straight one is that you take the filing and take twice its length between two healthy teeth, and then that you increase it with two tortuosities of the filing between two damaged ones, or if one or several, until the thread reaches the healthy tooth of the other part. And then iterate the placement within the part from which you began, and strengthen your hand with ease and skill so that it is not damaged.
And let your pliers with which you strengthen the filings be the roots of the teeth so that it does not escape.
And then incise the ends of the superfluous filings with the forceps or tweezers, and add those in each place with gesture, and turn them and hide them between the healthy tooth and the damaged tooth, so that it does not cause injury to the tongue. And then leave it so straight as a Roman.
But if it is loosened or broken, strengthen it or them with another filing in such a manner throughout its time.
And this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the straightness of two healthy teeth and two damaged ones, as well as these tied:
And when it is done that a tooth or two is returned to its place after the fall of each one, and they are regrown as we have recounted, and they remain.
And this is done only by a good artificer and wise.
And sometimes it is fitted some cause of the bones of cows, and it is made as the form of a tooth, and it is placed in the place where the tooth is missing, and it is strengthened as we have said, and it remains and serves with it for a long time.
Chapter .xxxiv.
Of the incision of the ligament which comes in the tongue and prohibits speech.
This ligament which comes from the tongue some times or is natural with which man is born, or accidental and caused by a plague which is already consolidated.
And the operation on it is that men open the mouth of the patient, his head existing in the tieu se; and elevate his tongue, and then incise that ligament nerve according to the latitude so that the tongue is released from its recess.
But if in that there is some hardness or knotting, and this is due to the consolidation of plague, then you put an incision and split that by the latitude while you have incised the ligament and the knot is dissolved.
And guard yourself that no fissure is made in the flesh of the jaw and that you split here the artery and blood comes.
And then wash the vestiges of the incision with water or with vinegar or with cold water; and then place under the tongue a linen; so is the way which holds the patient of the tongue in each night so that it is not consolidated another time.
But if blood flow occurs, place on the location vitriol trias; but if the blood comes, then cauterize the location with a cauterizing instrument which is convenient for this. And then this cure with the other causes so that it is healed.
Chapter .xxxv.
Of the extraction of a ranula from the tongue.
Sometimes a boil happens on the tongue resembling a small lump which prohibits the tongue from its natural operation; and it often grows larger while the mouth is open.
And the operation on it is that men open the mouth of the patient facing the sun and consider the boil.
And if you see it of dark color or of black, hard, which the patient does not feel, then do not touch that because it is a cancer.
And if it is inclined to whiteness, in which there is moisture, then you put the incision in it, and incise it with a subtle spatula, and split it from all parts; and if blood comes to you in the hour of your operation, then you place under it trias, which is vitriol, so that it restricts the blood.
And then return to your work while you had treated it with compliment of it, so that it is washed with vinegar and salt; and cure this with the other cure with water so that it is healed.
Chapter .xxxvi.
Of the extraction of a boil in the ears and of that which is nothing in the throat and of the other boils.
When in the throat a gland is swollen, so are the glands which are assembled swollen, which sometimes happen outside and are called boils, which when you cure them with water as we have said in the division and it is not healed, then consider if the boil is hard, of dark color, of little feeling, then do not touch that with iron.
And if it is of red color and the root is thick, then do not touch that with iron because of the flow of blood; let it lie there until it is matured, and then either you will extract it, or it will break by itself.
And if it is of white color, soft, and the root of it is subtle, then this is that it should be incised.
And the operation on it is that you consider, before your operation, if the boil has already rested of it covered with a complete rest or if it has diminished with some diminution; and then do that the patient stands before the sun, and the head of him is in the tieu se, and open the mouth of him, and the servant takes between his hands pressing the tongue of him with a noble instrument of which this is the form:
And it is made of silver or of brass, and it is subtle with a knife.

Other water that you pull some cause of the tunics, and then incise that with the instrument of which this is the form:
Other water that you pull some cause of the tunics, and then incise that with the instrument of which this is the form: And it is assembled like forceps, but the extremities of it are curved, so that the orifice of each one is in the straight of the other, very sharp, which should be of iron, indi embedded.
But if this instrument is not at your present, then incise that with a spatula of which this is the form of it: And it is sharp on one part, not sharp on the other part.
And because you have incised a furrow, incise the other according to this same manner of incision, and then the incision the patient should wash with cold water
But if there is a flow of blood, wash with water of decoction of the bark of millefolium or of myrtle leaf and similar to that of the stiptic causes so that the flow of blood is restricted, and then cure this until it is healed.
And sometimes there are found in the throat other boils besides those ear boils, and incise those according to what I have said in the incision of two furrows equally.
And I had once treated a woman with an abscess which was located in the throat of her, the abscess was of a dark brown color, of little feeling, which had already closed the throat of her, and the woman breathed with a tight chest, and had already prohibited her to eat and drink water, and she had already come to death if it had not been for a day or two.
And the abscess had grown so much that it had two fistfuls within it which came out through two openings.
Therefore, I cut it open fisturally and placed myself in one of the openings, and pulled out that one, and it came out with a large portion, and then I incised that one from where I understood the other opening, and then I opened the mouth of it, and compressed its tongue, and then I placed the opening in that abscess.
And then I drained a large portion of it, and it did not flow out except a little blood. Therefore, the throat of that woman was completely opened, and she began to drink water immediately, and then she ate food, therefore I did not cease to incise that abscess many times for a long time, and a new abscess succeeded in its place, which incision extended as long as that one.
Therefore, I brought a needle and cauterized the throat of her, so as to add no more; and then I walked away and did not know what God had done to her from that moment.
Chapter .xxxvii.
Of incision of a boil when it is an abscess.
When a catarr arises on the boil, and it is an abscess and it is long, then it is called a perpendicular; and if it is in the part below, thick and round, and then it is called a bubo.

Sometimes the uvula is cured with water that is more subtle than cauterization and incision, because it is cured with fumigation in this manner: Take calament, ysop, origua, ruda, sicados arabic, camomilla, broyda and similar to those of the herbs, and adjust all those causes, or some of them, in an olla, and be submerged with strong wine, and boil; and the olla be well washed with good lut, and be in the middle of the olla a hole, on which be placed an instrument concavity of ram according to this manner; be made of silver or of ram.

But if this instrument is not at your present, then take a cane and compose in the extremity of it a shell of wood, so that the mouth of the patient be covered, because the shell of wood prohibits the vapor from burning the mouth.
And this cure is good for health.
Chapter .xxxviii.
Of the extraction of thorns and of what adheres in the throat and of the other causes.
Moist things adhered in the throat or a thorn or any other cause.

Chapter .xxxix.
Of the extraction of bloodsucking annexed to the throat.
When the bloodsucker is medicated with what we have said in the division of the cure with medicines and does not confer, consider then in the throat of the patient to the sun, because you may have comprehended the tongue of him with the instrument which to you we have recommended.
Therefore, if you see the bloodsucker, extract it with a small hook or with a subtle gesture decently.
And if it is not possible to extract with that, then take a concave cannula and insert it into the throat of the patient, and then place in the concavity of the cannula a burning iron, and do this as many times (until the bloodsucker is dead and is removed from the throat) and abstain the patient all day of water.
And then put a vessel full of cold water, and work the mouth of him in that, and wash the mouth with that; and do not swallow any of that, and wipe the mouth with his hand one hour after another, because the bloodsucker as soon as it feels the water catches.
But if it is not thrown-up with what we have recommended, then fumigate the patient with cymint or with asafoetida by the instrument which we have recommended in the fumigation of the uvula.
Do this, so that it may fall.
And there is another way of operation in fumigation of that, which is that you take a bowl in which there are burning coals and the bowl is covered with a blanket in the middle of which there is a hole, and it is composed in that hole the extremity of the instrument; and then let down the fumigation; and place the patient's mouth at the extremity of the cannula, and close his mouth so that the fumigation is not thrown-up until you know that the fumigation has reached the bloodsucker, because the bloodsucker immediately falls.
And if it does not catch, then you repeat the fumigation many times, and abstain the patient from drinking, and eat salty and spicy things, and do not drink water, and thus necessarily it is that with this regimen it is thrown-up.
And this is the form of the instrument with which the bloodsucker of the throat is treated when it is seen; and it is similar to forceps as you see, unless that in it there is some curvature: Which is placed in the throat, and the extremity of it is similar to the beak of a stork, that is, it is blunt, in which it is sharpened by a file, so that, when we grasp any cause, it does not leave it.
Chapter .xl.
In which is the sum of the speech in the opening of abscesses and in their section.
Abscesses are special kinds, of many kinds, according to what we remember of them, of each one in this book.
And they are diverse in perforation and section of them by two ways, of which one is by the species of abscesses in themselves; and by that which we understand of the humidities.
And the second way is according to the places in which they occur in the body, for the abscess that occurs in the head is different from the abscess that occurs in the buttocks; and the abscess in the fleshy place is different from the abscess that occurs in the joint; and to each of them is its own way of operation.
And more than abscesses are some that ought not to be perforated but rather upon the maturation of the matter in them or the completion of them.
There are other abscesses that ought to be drained when they are ripe, and not upon the completion of them, such as abscesses that are near the joints, for when an abscess is near a joint, its being is prolonged until it can pour out what is in its circuit, and then it is very likely that the ligaments or nerves of that joint are corrupted, so that it becomes the cause of contraction of that limb; or it is an abscess near a principal member, and if you delay the perforation of it until it is mature, it will harm the principal member; or it is near the buttocks, therefore perforate it before it is mature; and you ought not to perforate it raw, of incomplete digestion, but the one that is near the buttocks, so that you cannot scratch the perineum of it and extend it to the parts around the buttocks, and make a fistula, or that it be made in the term of it that it not be healed. But more, you ought to know the hour of the perforation of the abscess, and thus it is when it is mature.
And you ought to know that it is mature when there is the cessation of pain and the cessation of fever, and about the diminution of the heat and of the pulse, and the sharpness of the head of the abscess, and the other signs.
And that you ought to know the perforation to be made in the place farthest from the abscess and from pus coming from the cure of the eminence.
And perforation always be by the length of the flesh or of the body, if the abscesses are in the parts of the limbs or of the feet, and in places of the tendons, of the nerves, of the arteries; and, in the end, in all places equal in which there is no reflection; for in those that are reflected, use of perforation according to that limb.
But when the abscess is in a fleshy place, then it is best that you let the perforation of it until the digestion of it is confirmed according to its completion, as we have said; for if you perforate it before that, it prolongates the course of the pus of it and of much filth, and then very likely the lips of it are hardened and the depth of it.
But some abscesses are perforated according to the latitude of the flesh or of the body, according to the necessity, or according to what the limb requires.
And you ought to administer small perforation, and in the large abscesses, large perforation and many sections according to the diversity of the greatness of the abscesses.
And others are of the abscesses in which the wound ought to be concave and be incised, when it is made so that it is like bread and it is made in a term that it already sticks, like that which occurs in too many boils and buboes.
And of those are those that are incised with section having three angles; and of those it is in the one that is incised like the figure of a myrtle leaf, like the abscesses of the angles.
And of those are those in which a round section and a lunar section, and similar to those, are administered.
But that one to which there is no such as his abscesses are superficial, you ought to perforate that with superficial perforation, or flat only.
And you ought when the abscess is large and has already collected much matter, that you perforate that and do not take that you extract all the pus in that hour; having extracted from it one part, and about close the abscess until the next day, and about extract a larger part, and about do that many times according to the graduation until it is finished.
And more so if the patient is of cold virtue, or woman pregnant, or little child, or old in decrepitude, for the animal spirit many times is resolved with the egress of the matter, and very likely the patient dies, and you operate on them.
Therefore, guard this chapter with great care, and about the perforation in which you perforate these abscesses, you ought to abstain from the plagues and consider therefore if the plague of the abscess is little, or is a flat section, then you administer the qualms of it or of a counter-coction; and if the abscess is large, and the fissures of the perforation are many, then you ought to place a poultice in each one until they come together.
And if in the abscess is abscinded a part of the wound or you have concaved that in the circuit, then you ought to cover it with a poultice of old cloth or of a thread made of cloth of it, as when you have treated bread or roots, its humidity; and strengthen that until the third day; and about process that and cure it with that which you ought of the poultices until it is healed.
But if blood flows during the operation, then you administer cold water and vinegar to the cloths, and place that on the location of the blood flow many times.
But if the blood flow persists, then it is necessary that you administer regimen and cure and powders which I have recommended in many places of this our book and of division.
But if it is in wintertime, and the location of the abscess is a place of many nerves, then you must enfund pulvils in vinegar and olive oil caut, and place those on the locations.
And if it is in summer, and the locations are fleshy, then you must place powders soaked in water and oil or in vinegar and oil, and all that be cold until the third day, as we have said, and then you must open the abscess and cleanse that and administer in its cure what is convenient to it until it is healed.
And thus is what is necessary of the knowledge of the cure of abscesses universally, but according to the way of distinction I have already said of every abscess in what manner is the way of its cure by chapters singularly.
Chapter .xli.
Of the section of abscesses which come in the neck of the head.
In the neck of the head small abscesses, and so of species of nodes which contain tunics which are to their making; and the species of them are many.
And of them are pimples, and of those are those which contain humidity similar to lime. And of those are those which contain humidity similar to dust, and resembling to them; and of those are those which are stony, hard.
And in the section of all, and in the extraction of those there is no fear, as you must the exterior of those does not make contrary artery.
And the operation in section of those is that you probe those with an instrument the shape of which comes close thus, the one which is called entromes, as long as you know that it contains.
Because if that which contains is humidity, then you split that with section according to the length by superficial section according to this form:
And beginning in the section of the line of .B. into the line of .G. Therefore as the humidity is evacuated, then you excoriate that peel which contains that humidity, and do not leave of that any cause of all, because troops many times return, if remain of that any cause.
And then you submerge the throat in Egyptian enguent, if it is present, and if not, in water and salt; and fill with that the wound and leave it in for another day, because with that you corrode all that is remaining of that pellicle.
And then repeat on that throat with Egyptian enguent second and third time if you indigesties of it, as long as you trust that there was no remaining any cause of that pellicle; then cure the wound with enguent until it is healed.
And if abscess contains fatty nodes, then you incise that according to this form: with a section having the form of a cross, and get oncis between two lips of the section and scorsa that of all parts, and exert your virtue in the extraction of the tunic which contains that.
But if to your artery makes contrariety, then do what I have told you first.
And similarly do in the lapificated abscess of section and cure according to that we have told you; and section on lapificated abscess is lighter, because it is of little blood and of little humidity.
And some times there are some of these abscesses which are in the head in some men with which of all there is no humidity; the cause of which is because I incised upon an abscess in the head of an old woman and retrieved the abscess thus as a hard, rough, white, which could not be drained, and if to someone it was struck with that, it would plague that person.
But in the other abscesses accidents in the head other this is not this chapter, as well as the abscesses that come to the heads of the children and you must the roots of the ears, but the section of these all is superficial.
And pause the perforation of those of the lower part of them so that the body of the blood be relieved in the lower parts.
And then cure those with what is convenient to that of cure.
Chapter .xlii.
Of the section of scrophulas which happen in the neck.
Many times these abscesses become in the neck and in the armpits and in the groin; and some times happen in the other parts of the body.
And are those that happen in the neck, and so many that are engendered between them, and all scrofula of those is within its own tunic, and as in the nodes and abscesses of the head, as we have recommended.
And the species of these scrophulas are many, because of those some are stony, and of those some contain humidities, and of those are malignant the ones which do not obey to cure.
Therefore in that which you see of good disposition in the Touch, of which the color of that which is manifest is proper to the color of the neck, and is good all over, and is not annexed to the nerve of the neck, nor to the veins, nor to the artery, and is not swollen, then you must incise that with superficial section from the lower part to the upper part of the body of the line of .G. into the line of .B., and scorsa that of all parts, and extend the lips of the neck with onci, or with many oncis if you have need of those, as we have said in the abscesses of the head, and extract that little by little.
And it is more caution that the vein or nerve is not incised.
And let the spatula not be too sharp, that it does not hurt your hand with incision, or that it frightens the patient, and that you cut what is not necessary to cut; for if you were to cut a vein or artery and you prohibit yourself from your operation, then pause in the plague with vitriol or other powders which stop the flow of blood, and tighten the plague, and leave that which is inside that the sharpness of the abscess is paused and the plague is softened and begins to be pus-filled. When the blood is cut.
Therefore, return to your operation before you have completed it.
And then inquire with your little finger if there is any cause of the other small abscesses, therefore cut those and clean them.
And if it is at the root of the large abscess, cover it so that you do not cut that abscess from its root. Cover it so that you place that with a bent iron and let it fall by itself, so that it does no harm.
And then fill the wound with old cloth which you have already submerged in Egyptian ointment, and then cure it.
And if you cut that abscess entirely, then cover it so that you adjust the two lips of the wound and close it as quickly as possible so that there is no superfluity of pus.
But if you see that there is superfluity due to the size of the abscess, cover it so that you understand to cut the root of it, and extract it and administer suture and what is said.
And those of the abscesses that contain humidity, pierce it with a superficial puncture where you see the place of maturation of it, and place a puncture of what is the pus from the bottom of the body, as we have said.
And then administer puncture, calms with ointment and similar things to those, so that it corrodes what is rotten from the corruption. And then when you see the wound already cleaned, then cure it with ointment of generative flesh until it is healed.
Chapter .xliii.
Of the section of the abscess of the pile within the gullet.
The ancients said this section in the pile, and no one has seen in our land that it has been done.
And this is the inscription of the sermon of those.
But in men having a hernia, cover that it be avoided the extraction of the pile, as for that it is not done well because all the veins and the major parts of the body are here.
But in those who have abscesses caused in the mouth or gullet or both ears, when the disease is not in the canal, cover to use the section of the pile to avoid the damage which is done by puncture.
Therefore, when we want this, that they cut the pile below three circles of the circles of the pile, or four with a small section for the latitude in that which is between two circles for quantity, that the section be in the flesh, not in the cartilage, and this place is convenient for section, because it is deprived of flesh and the blood vessels of it are there.
And if the doctor is fearful, then cover that he extend the throat of the gullet with a clamp, and then cut the throat until it reaches the canal, but avoid the blood vessels if you see any cause of those.
And then cut the flesh according to what we have recommended; and it is significant over the section of the canal by the flame which is of that which is emitted with what is of it disrupted and by the abscess of the voice.
And leave the wound open for some time.
Therefore, as the hour is renewed in which puncture is feared, add two lips of the throat of the wound, and sew that alone if it is the cartilage.
And then administer medicines that make flesh grow until it is healed.
And Albucasis says that the sum of the sermon which we have recommended, exposition is not but that you see that some of these abscesses have already opened the gullet of the patient, and the patient has come to death, and the skin of it is dried, and some go to cut the epiglottis so that the patient breathes over the place of the wound by any breathing, and be saved from death.
And for that reason, command to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease is consumed; and the malice of it is for three days; and then command so the wound, and cure it until it is healed.
And what I have seen with my own eyes, is that a servant took a knife and put it in her throat and cut with it a part of the canal of the lung, and I was called to the cure of her, and I brought back the woman as if she was dying, and I uncovered the wound and brought back the blood which was coming out of the wound small.
Therefore, I was confessed that she had not cut a vein nor guidegi, and the wind was coming out of the wound, and I cured her until she was healed.
And I did not accuse the servant if not that she was hoarse in the voice, and after some days returned to the improvement of her dispositions.
And now I say that in the section of the epilhot there is no fear.
Chapter XLIV.
Of incision over an abscess which happens in the throat outside, and is called a hernia of the throat.
This abscess called a hernia of the throat is a large abscess according to the color of the body, and it moves in women.
And it is according to two manners, whether it is natural or accidental.
And in the natural one it is not a matter of curing.
And the accidental one is according to two manners, of which one is similar to fatty nodes, and the other manner is similar to an abscess which is made by the knotting of an artery, and in that one there is fear. And no cove that one should make presumption about it, like iron, but in the one that is small. And you probe that one and investigate that one with the finger, and if you find that one similar to a fatty node, and it is not suspended by any of the veins, then you incise that one as well as the nodes, and extract that one with what contains it from the skin and bursa; and if not, then you scrutinize the whole of its being, and then cure the place with what is necessary for healing before it is healed.
Chapter XLV.
Of incision of the kinds of nodes.
Of nodes there are many kinds and I have already said all the kinds of them in the division.
And I must recount thus the difference between a node and an exulceration as if making a doubt.
Therefore I say that in an exulceration there is heat and fever and violent pains until the boiling of the superfluity is subsided; and it is complicated putrefaction that at the hour ceases the fever, the pain, and the heat.
But in a node there is no heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains that which is in the sac proper to it.
And it is according to the color of the body, and the beginning of it is like a boil and it is made as well as a cyst, whether it is larger or smaller, and they are according to two kinds, whether they are fatty and contain humidity, and the colors of the humidity are many, according to what I said in the division.
Therefore, when you arrive at the cure of a node, that you examine it and inquire about it at the beginning with the instrument which is called an intromes, according to what will come its form in the chapter which is about this.
And this manner of inquiry of abscesses and of all nodes, and it is that you take this instrument and introduce it into the place most humid which you find in the abscess, and you revolve your fingers with it little by little until you know that the instrument has already penetrated the cord.
And then last your hand according to the measure of the greatness of the abscess, and then extract the intromes and consider what is issued in the vestige of it.
And if the humidity is flowing out, of whatever color it may be, then you incise it with a superficial incision according to what I have said in the other abscesses.
And if from the vestige of the intromes there is no humidity, then you know that it is fatty.
And dry over it with an incision having the shape of a cross according to this shape: as well as I have taught you, and suspend that with pins, and excoriate the cord from every part with facility, and guard the skin or sac, if you can, over it and extract that sania with the node.
But if it is broken in the operation, it is not possible to extract that sania, and many times it must be so, and then you extract it in pieces until nothing of it remains.
For if from it remains nothing, little or much, the node returns according to the most.
And if you see that from it remains any small part, then fill the wound with some sharp corrosive powders and strengthen the wound, and place over it a cautery of the abscess, and cure it with the other cure until it is healed.
And if it is a large node, then you sew the two lips of it and cure it with what encases.
But if a pulsatile vein is in it opposite, or non-pulsatile, then you cover and poultice the place with thrice-beaten vitriol and leave it straight for two or three days until you can re-open the wound and that the boiling of the blood is calmed; and then return to incise that which is broken from the node.

Chapter .xlvii.
Of the cure of the breasts of men which are assembled from women.
Sometimes the breasts of certain men become inflamed due to the way they sleep, and as they begin to be hairy, and then the breasts become inflamed, and the breasts are assembled like those of women, and are removed, pus is released.
And to him who suffers this, it is necessary that he incisions those areas with a lunar section according to this form, from the line of B. into the line of G., and then scrape the entire thickness, and then fill the wound with a medicinal ointment, and then adjust the two lips of the wound with sewing, and care for him until it is healed.
But if the breast declines to the sides and is softened by its magnitude as it should be in women, then it is cut in two halves, its pus being removed, with two sections similar to the lunar figure, of which each one contains the other, as long as the larger line contains the smaller one according to this form of the line of B. and the line of G. And then scrape the tissue which is between the two lips of the wound, and remove the fat, and administer what we have said about suturing and the powders, what is necessary for the healing until it is healed.
And if you do not comply with the incision of what needs to be incised because of the restlessness of the patient, and the flow of blood, then you must fill the wound with a cloth submerged in corrosive liquid and leave it until what corrodes is removed from the gray matter, and then care for him until it is healed.
Chapter .xlviii.
Of the perforation of abscesses that come from the nipple.
These abscesses that come from the nipple are of the kind of scrophulas, hard, which contain a skin that is sac.
And of these there are some that contain humidity; and those that contain humidity must be incised with a lunar section according to this figure: from the line of G. to the line of B. And as soon as everything that is in the abscess of the healthy is evacuated, then you fill it with old cloth and leave it for the next day.
And then the cloth is removed and it is cured with a suitable ointment to the water, until it is healed.
And if the abscess is of the kind of nodes and scrophulas, then you cut it as we have said in the section on scrophulas in the same way.
But if the wound is extended in such a way that it is a cavity, then administer to it cautery according to what we have said before.
Chapter .xlix.
Of the incision of abscesses that occur due to artery or vein.
When an artery is ruptured, and the tissue that is above it is consolidated, then often abscesses occur. And the signs by which it is known that inflammation and abscess are due to the artery or vein: because when an abscess is due to the artery, it is long attached in the front of the body; and that when you pierce the abscess with your fingers, you feel in it a kind of hissing sound.
And that which is due to the vein is red and apparent on the surface of the body.
And the incision on this abscess is an error, and most of all in that which is in the armpits, and in the corners, and in the neck, and in most places of the body; and it is very large, therefore it is necessary that its cure with iron be avoided, and that which is in the extremities, or in the head, it should be avoided.
But on that which is of them due to the inflammation of the orifice of the artery, cut in the tissue a long incision; and then probe the incision with probes and then the artery, and deliver from the tunics until it is uncovered.
And then place on that needle and make it penetrate into the other side, and tighten the artery with a double thread in two places — which causes you to see the extraction of two arteries which are in the temples.
And then prick the place which is between the two ligaments with a spatula until all the blood that is in it is extracted, and the abscess is dissolved.
And then administer a cure in which power is generated until the ligaments fall; and then care for him with suitable ointments to the water until it is healed.
And if the abscess is due to the section of a vein, then you must have in your hand that which is possible of the abscess with the tissue, and then introduce the needle from the place which you have had in your hand, and make it penetrate; and be in that double thread until you extract it from the other side, and then tie the abscess with a good ligament according to what I have told you in the ligament of the grape of two parts with two extremities of the thread.
But if you fear that the thread will be extracted, then introduce the needle with that needle into the whole abscess, and then tighten your threads in four places.
Then dry the abscess in the middle of it until when it is said that the water that is in it is gone, then you cut the superfluity of the tissue, and leave what of it is tied.
And then place on it a powder which you have submerged in wine and oil, and then administer the cure which is made with calxes and ointments until it is healed.
Chapter 1 of the abscess which happens by twisting of nerves.
Thus as abscesses occur in arteries and veins, and seemingly abscesses occur in nerves when they are struck or occur due to excessive labor, and in a similar manner.
And it is made most in the places of the auxiliaries or the talus, or in any place where the joints are maimed.
And it is a serious abscess, and it is assembled to the color of the other body, and in the majority of its dispositions it is of its own and when it is tightly squeezed with vehemence, the patient feels in it a semblance of stupor.
And it is not an abscess aggravated in the front of the body, and for this reason it is left the chain, and it is maimed in every part and does not go to the parts in front or behind.
Therefore, of those that are in the joints, it is not necessary that they be enclosed with iron, because it very quickly becomes a cause of contraction.
But the one that is in the head or in the front, finish the chain with a spatula. But if it is a small abscess, then take it with the forceps and excise it from the root.
And if it is large, then you suspend it with a hook, and excise it, and then you cover it; and adjust the poultice with suture, and care for it until it is healed.
Chapter .li.
Of the section of an abscess which happens from the cheek that happens to the belly.
And it happens to some men, growths in the bellies of those and in other parts of the body of those, the ones that are called fungous due to a similarity to those with fungi, of which the root is subtle and the head of it is thick; and already the lips of those are turned, and it is of those that are small, and it is of those that are much magnified.
And I have already seen one, and in the belly of him there were two parts the ones that were more like fungi, and there was no difference between those white, of fine root.
And already the lips of those were reversed and they were splitting, and humidity ran from that all the time.
Therefore, I incised those and attributed in the one in a weight of 18 ounces. and the other of 6 ounces.
And the operation in the incision of them is that you consider it, if the patient is humid, and the color of the one is white, humid, of subtle root; then you excise it with a spatula wide, and be in your presence cauterize in the fire, because many times the blood of the section of it is expelled much; and if you see the blood, cauterize it.
